{'role': 'user', 'content': 'Okay, now we need to work on the user interface. I would prefer an open design instead of a closed ecosystem with a bunch of navigation options.\n\nthe interface should be simple with an AI chat bot. There should be an on-boarding process to enter in information about the patient. There should be a seperate section to upload documents, such as PDFs. The AI chatbot will use a lower grade AI solultion. \n\nHowever, the analysis and other important tasks will use a large LLM that is HIPAA approved. My thought is using Azure (or whatever other cloud services that are HIPAA approved) that is spun up to do the work needed. \n\nWe will need a HIPAA-approved LLM, in addition to the HIPAA-approved cloud provider. The virtual instance is spun up to do the work, then de-provisioned until the next task.\n\nFor the context piece, we need to ensure that the AI prompts will allow the LLM to process using the available resources. For example, if the LLM is 8b or 12b, then the repository will optimize for the context window. In order to control costs, we will utilize the most efficient LLM (ie. Chatgpt 5, etc). \n\nIf the AI needs to split up the prompts to fit the context window, we can run different instances or have a que system.'}

Keep interface open and uncluttered\n\n## Responsive Design\n\n**Mobile-First Approach:**\n- Full-screen chat interface on mobile\n- Swipe gestures for navigation\n- Bottom navigation bar for key actions\n- Optimized for one-handed use\n\n**Tablet/Desktop:**\n- Wider chat interface with document preview\n- Side-by-side document viewing\n- Enhanced upload interface with drag-and-drop\n\n## Accessibility\n\n- WCAG 2.1 AA compliance\n- Screen reader support\n- Keyboard navigation\n- High contrast mode\n- Adjustable font sizes\n- Voice input support\n\n## Color Scheme\n\n**Primary Colors:**\n- Primary: #0066CC (Trust, Medical)\n- Secondary: #00A86B (Health, Wellness)\n- Accent: #FF6B35 (Alerts, Important)\n- Background: #FFFFFF (Clean, Medical)\n- Text: #1A1A1A (High contrast)\n\n**Status Colors:**\n- Success: #00A86B\n- Warning: #FFA500\n- Error: #DC3545\n- Info: #0066CC\n- Processing: #6C757D\n\n## Typography\n\n- **Headings:** Inter (Sans-serif, clean, modern)\n- **Body:** Inter (Consistent, readable)\n- **Monospace:** JetBrains Mono (Code, IDs)\n\n## Component Library\n\n**Using Radix UI + Tailwind CSS:**\n- Accessible by default\n- Customizable\n- Lightweight\n- Well-documented\n\n## Key UI Principles\n\n1. **Simplicity First** - Remove unnecessary elements\n2. **AI-Driven Navigation** - Let chat guide users\n3. **Progressive Disclosure** - Show advanced features only when needed\n4. **Immediate Feedback** - Real-time status updates\n5. **Trust & Security** - Clear security indicators\n6. **Mobile-Optimized** - Touch-friendly, responsive\n7. **Fast Loading** - Optimized performance\n8. **Clear CTAs** - Obvious next steps\n\n## User Flows\n\n### Primary Flow: Ask a Question\n```\nUser lands on dashboard â†’ Types question in chat â†’\nLightweight AI responds immediately â†’\n[If needed] Escalates to deep analysis â†’\nUser receives comprehensive answer\n```\n\n### Secondary Flow: Upload Document\n```\nUser clicks upload â†’ Selects/drags file â†’\nDocument uploads with progress indicator â†’\nAI automatically analyzes â†’\nUser receives notification when complete â†’\nUser can view analysis in chat\n```\n\n### Tertiary Flow: View Analysis\n```\nUser clicks on document â†’\nAnalysis summary displayed â†’\nChat interface shows key findings â†’\nUser can ask follow-up questions â†’\nAI provides detailed explanations\n```\n\n## Implementation Priority\n\n**Phase 1: Core Interface (Week 1-2)**\n- Dashboard layout\n- Chat interface\n- Basic navigation\n- Authentication screens\n\n**Phase 2: Onboarding (Week 3)**\n- Multi-step onboarding flow\n- Identity verification\n- Health profile setup\n- Document upload\n\n**Phase 3: Document Management (Week 4)**\n- Upload interface\n- Document list\n- Status tracking\n- Analysis viewing\n\n**Phase 4: Polish & Optimization (Week 5-6)**\n- Responsive design\n- Accessibility\n- Performance optimization\n- User testing & refinement\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

                                          â”‚\nâ””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜\n```\n\n## Component Details\n\n### 1. Lightweight Chatbot (Tier 1)\n\n**Purpose:** Handle 80% of user interactions with fast, cost-effective responses\n\n**Technology Stack:**\n- **Model:** OpenAI GPT-3.5 Turbo (4k context)\n- **Hosting:** Always-on API endpoint (Next.js API route)\n- **Response Time:** <2 seconds\n- **Cost:** ~$0.002 per interaction\n\n**Capabilities:**\n- General health questions\n- Medication reminders\n- Appointment scheduling\n- Navigation assistance\n- Document upload guidance\n- Quick lookups (symptoms, medications)\n- Conversational interface\n\n**Limitations:**\n- No PHI processing\n- No deep medical analysis\n- No document analysis\n- Limited context window\n\n**Implementation:**\n\n```typescript\n// services/LightweightChatbotService.ts\n\ninterface ChatbotConfig {\n  model: \'gpt-3.5-turbo\';\n  maxTokens: 500;\n  temperature: 0.7;\n  systemPrompt: string;\n}\n\ninterface ChatbotResponse {\n  message: string;\n  needsEscalation: boolean;\n  escalationReason?: string;\n  confidence: number;\n}\n\nclass LightweightChatbotService {\n  private config: ChatbotConfig = {\n    model: \'gpt-3.5-turbo\',\n    maxTokens: 500,\n    temperature: 0.7,\n    systemPrompt: `You are a helpful health assistant for HoloVitals. \n    You provide general health information, help with navigation, and answer \n    basic questions. For complex medical analysis or document review, \n    escalate to the deep analysis system. Never provide medical diagnoses \n    or treatment recommendations - always recommend consulting healthcare \n    providers for medical advice.`\n  };\n\n  async chat(\n    userId: string,\n    message: string,\n    conversationHistory: ChatMessage[]\n  ): Promise<ChatbotResponse> {\n    // Check if escalation is needed\n    const escalationCheck = this.shouldEscalate(message);\n    \n    if (escalationCheck.shouldEscalate) {\n      return {\n        message: "I\'ll connect you with our deep analysis system for a comprehensive review.",\n        needsEscalation: true,\n        escalationReason: escalationCheck.reason,\n        confidence: 1.0\n      };\n    }\n\n    // Generate response using GPT-3.5\n    const response = await this.generateResponse(message, conversationHistory);\n    \n    return {\n      message: response.content,\n      needsEscalation: false,\n      confidence: response.confidence\n    };\n  }\n\n  private shouldEscalate(message: string): {\n    shouldEscalate: boolean;\n    reason?: string;\n  } {\n    const escalationKeywords = [\n      \'analyze document\',\n      \'review my labs\',\n      \'interpret results\',\n      \'diagnosis\',\n      \'treatment plan\',\n      \'medical opinion\',\n      \'compare my results\'\n    ];\n\n    const lowerMessage = message.toLowerCase();\n    \n    for (const keyword of escalationKeywords) {\n      if (lowerMessage.includes(keyword)) {\n        return {\n          shouldEscalate: true,\n          reason: `Complex query requiring deep analysis: ${keyword}`\n        };\n      }\n    }\n\n    return { shouldEscalate: false };\n  }\n\n  private async generateResponse(\n    message: string,\n    history: ChatMessage[]\n  ): Promise<{ content: string; confidence: number }> {\n    // Implementation using OpenAI API\n    // Returns quick, general responses\n    return {\n      content: "Generated response",\n      confidence: 0.85\n    };\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 2. Heavy-Duty Analysis Engine (Tier 2)\n\n**Purpose:** Deep medical document analysis, complex queries, comprehensive insights\n\n**Technology Stack:**\n- **Models:** GPT-4 Turbo, Claude 3 Opus/Sonnet, Llama 3 70B\n- **Hosting:** Ephemeral cloud instances (Azure/AWS)\n- **Response Time:** 5-30 minutes\n- **Cost:** $0.50-$5.00 per analysis (depending on complexity)\n\n**Capabilities:**\n- Full medical document analysis\n- Multi-document comparison\n- Trend analysis over time\n- Complex medical reasoning\n- Detailed recommendations\n- Risk assessment\n- Drug interaction analysis\n\n**HIPAA Compliance:**\n- Azure Health Data Services\n- AWS HealthLake\n- Encrypted data in transit and at rest\n- Audit logging\n- Access controls\n- PHI sanitization before caching\n\n### 3. Context Window Optimization\n\n**Problem:** Large documents may exceed LLM context windows\n\n**Solution:** Intelligent prompt splitting and parallel processing\n\n```typescript\n// services/ContextOptimizerService.ts\n\ninterface ContextAnalysis {\n  totalTokens: number;\n  contextWindow: number;\n  needsSplitting: boolean;\n  splitStrategy?: \'sequential\' | \'parallel\' | \'hierarchical\';\n  estimatedCost: number;\n  recommendedModel: string;\n}\n\ninterface PromptSplit {\n  id: string;\n  content: string;\n  tokens: number;\n  order: number;\n  dependencies: string[];\n}\n\nclass ContextOptimizerService {\n  // Model context windows\n  private modelContextWindows = {\n    \'gpt-4-turbo\': 128000,\n    \'gpt-4\': 8192,\n    \'claude-3-opus\': 200000,\n    \'claude-3-sonnet\': 200000,\n    \'llama-3-70b\': 8192\n  };\n\n  // Model costs per 1M tokens (input/output)\n  private modelCosts = {\n    \'gpt-4-turbo\': { input: 10, output: 30 },\n    \'gpt-4\': { input: 30, output: 60 },\n    \'claude-3-opus\': { input: 15, output: 75 },\n    \'claude-3-sonnet\': { input: 3, output: 15 },\n    \'llama-3-70b\': { input: 0.9, output: 0.9 } // Self-hosted estimate\n  };\n\n  async analyzeContext(\n    documents: string[],\n    analysisType: string\n  ): Promise<ContextAnalysis> {\n    // Calculate total tokens\n    const totalTokens = this.estimateTokens(documents.join(\'\\n\'));\n    \n    // Select optimal model\n    const recommendedModel = this.selectOptimalModel(totalTokens, analysisType);\n    const contextWindow = this.modelContextWindows[recommendedModel];\n    \n    // Determine if splitting is needed\n    const needsSplitting = totalTokens > (contextWindow * 0.8); // 80% threshold\n    \n    // Calculate estimated cost\n    const estimatedCost = this.calculateCost(\n      totalTokens,\n      recommendedModel,\n      needsSplitting\n    );\n\n    return {\n      totalTokens,\n      contextWindow,\n      needsSplitting,\n      splitStrategy: needsSplitting ? this.determineSplitStrategy(analysisType) : undefined,\n      estimatedCost,\n      recommendedModel\n    };\n  }\n\n  async splitPrompt(\n    content: string,\n    contextWindow: number,\n    strategy: \'sequential\' | \'parallel\' | \'hierarchical\'\n  ): Promise<PromptSplit[]> {\n    const tokens = this.estimateTokens(content);\n    const maxTokensPerSplit = Math.floor(contextWindow * 0.7); // Leave room for system prompt\n\n    if (strategy === \'sequential\') {\n      return this.splitSequentially(content, maxTokensPerSplit);\n    } else if (strategy === \'parallel\') {\n      return this.splitInParallel(content, maxTokensPerSplit);\n    } else {\n      return this.splitHierarchically(content, maxTokensPerSplit);\n    }\n  }\n\n  private selectOptimalModel(\n    tokens: number,\n    analysisType: string\n  ): string {\n    // Priority: Cost efficiency > Context window > Performance\n    \n    if (tokens < 7000) {\n      // Small documents - use most cost-efficient\n      return \'llama-3-70b\'; // or \'claude-3-sonnet\'\n    } else if (tokens < 100000) {\n      // Medium documents - balance cost and performance\n      return \'gpt-4-turbo\';\n    } else {\n      // Large documents - need large context window\n      return \'claude-3-opus\';\n    }\n  }\n\n  private determineSplitStrategy(analysisType: string): \'sequential\' | \'parallel\' | \'hierarchical\' {\n    // Sequential: For time-series data, chronological analysis\n    // Parallel: For independent sections (multiple lab reports)\n    // Hierarchical: For complex documents with subsections\n\n    if (analysisType.includes(\'timeline\') || analysisType.includes(\'trend\')) {\n      return \'sequential\';\n    } else if (analysisType.includes(\'compare\') || analysisType.includes(\'multiple\')) {\n      return \'parallel\';\n    } else {\n      return \'hierarchical\';\n    }\n  }\n\n  private splitSequentially(content: string, maxTokens: number): PromptSplit[] {\n    // Split content into sequential chunks\n    const chunks: PromptSplit[] = [];\n    let currentChunk = \'\';\n    let currentTokens = 0;\n    let order = 0;\n\n    const paragraphs = content.split(\'\\n\\n\');\n\n    for (const paragraph of paragraphs) {\n      const paragraphTokens = this.estimateTokens(paragraph);\n\n      if (currentTokens + paragraphTokens > maxTokens) {\n        // Save current chunk\n        chunks.push({\n          id: `chunk-${order}`,\n          content: currentChunk,\n          tokens: currentTokens,\n          order: order,\n          dependencies: order > 0 ? [`chunk-${order - 1}`] : []\n        });\n\n        // Start new chunk\n        currentChunk = paragraph;\n        currentTokens = paragraphTokens;\n        order++;\n      } else {\n        currentChunk += \'\\n\\n\' + paragraph;\n        currentTokens += paragraphTokens;\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Add final chunk\n    if (currentChunk) {\n      chunks.push({\n        id: `chunk-${order}`,\n        content: currentChunk,\n        tokens: currentTokens,\n        order: order,\n        dependencies: order > 0 ? [`chunk-${order - 1}`] : []\n      });\n    }\n\n    return chunks;\n  }\n\n  private splitInParallel(content: string, maxTokens: number): PromptSplit[] {\n    // Split content into independent parallel chunks\n    // Each chunk can be processed simultaneously\n    const chunks: PromptSplit[] = [];\n    const sections = this.identifySections(content);\n\n    let order = 0;\n    for (const section of sections) {\n      const sectionTokens = this.estimateTokens(section);\n\n      if (sectionTokens <= maxTokens) {\n        chunks.push({\n          id: `section-${order}`,\n          content: section,\n          tokens: sectionTokens,\n          order: order,\n          dependencies: [] // No dependencies - can run in parallel\n        });\n        order++;\n      } else {\n        // Section too large - split further\n        const subChunks = this.splitSequentially(section, maxTokens);\n        chunks.push(...subChunks.map(chunk => ({\n          ...chunk,\n          id: `section-${order}-${chunk.id}`,\n          order: order\n        })));\n        order++;\n      }\n    }\n\n    return chunks;\n  }\n\n  private splitHierarchically(content: string, maxTokens: number): PromptSplit[] {\n    // Create hierarchical structure: summary â†’ details\n    const chunks: PromptSplit[] = [];\n\n    // First pass: Create summary\n    const summary = this.extractSummary(content);\n    chunks.push({\n      id: \'summary\',\n      content: summary,\n      tokens: this.estimateTokens(summary),\n      order: 0,\n      dependencies: []\n    });\n\n    // Second pass: Split detailed sections\n    const sections = this.identifySections(content);\n    let order = 1;\n\n    for (const section of sections) {\n      const sectionTokens = this.estimateTokens(section);\n\n      if (sectionTokens <= maxTokens) {\n        chunks.push({\n          id: `detail-${order}`,\n          content: section,\n          tokens: sectionTokens,\n          order: order,\n          dependencies: [\'summary\'] // Depends on summary\n        });\n        order++;\n      }\n    }\n\n    return chunks;\n  }\n\n  private estimateTokens(text: string): number {\n    // Rough estimation: 1 token â‰ˆ 4 characters\n    return Math.ceil(text.length / 4);\n  }\n\n  private identifySections(content: string): string[] {\n    // Identify logical sections in document\n    // Look for headers, page breaks, etc.\n    return content.split(/\\n#{1,3}\\s+/);\n  }\n\n  private extractSummary(content: string): string {\n    // Extract or generate summary of content\n    // Take first few paragraphs or key sections\n    const paragraphs = content.split(\'\\n\\n\');\n    return paragraphs.slice(0, 3).join(\'\\n\\n\');\n  }\n\n  private calculateCost(\n    tokens: number,\n    model: string,\n    needsSplitting: boolean\n  ): number {\n    const costs = this.modelCosts[model];\n    const inputCost = (tokens / 1000000) * costs.input;\n    const outputCost = (tokens * 0.3 / 1000000) * costs.output; // Assume 30% output\n\n    if (needsSplitting) {\n      // Add overhead for splitting (multiple API calls)\n      return (inputCost + outputCost) * 1.5;\n    }\n\n    return inputCost + outputCost;\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 4. Queue System\n\n**Purpose:** Manage analysis tasks efficiently with priority handling\n\n```typescript\n// services/AnalysisQueueService.ts\n\nenum QueuePriority {\n  URGENT = 1,    // <5 minutes\n  HIGH = 2,      // <15 minutes\n  NORMAL = 3,    // <30 minutes\n  LOW = 4        // <60 minutes\n}\n\ninterface QueueTask {\n  id: string;\n  userId: string;\n  type: \'document_analysis\' | \'complex_query\' | \'comparison\' | \'trend_analysis\';\n  priority: QueuePriority;\n  documents: string[];\n  prompt: string;\n  contextAnalysis: ContextAnalysis;\n  status: \'queued\' | \'processing\' | \'completed\' | \'failed\';\n  createdAt: Date;\n  startedAt?: Date;\n  completedAt?: Date;\n  result?: any;\n  error?: string;\n}\n\nclass AnalysisQueueService {\n  async addToQueue(task: Omit<QueueTask, \'id\' | \'status\' | \'createdAt\'>): Promise<string> {\n    const queueTask: QueueTask = {\n      ...task,\n      id: this.generateTaskId(),\n      status: \'queued\',\n      createdAt: new Date()\n    };\n\n    // Add to database queue\n    await prisma.analysisQueue.create({\n      data: queueTask\n    });\n\n    // Notify user\n    await this.notifyUser(task.userId, \'queued\', queueTask.id);\n\n    // Trigger processing\n    await this.processQueue();\n\n    return queueTask.id;\n  }\n\n  async processQueue(): Promise<void> {\n    // Get next task by priority\n    const task = await this.getNextTask();\n\n    if (!task) return;\n\n    try {\n      // Update status\n      await this.updateTaskStatus(task.id, \'processing\');\n\n      // Provision instance and execute\n      const result = await this.executeAnalysis(task);\n\n      // Update with result\n      await this.updateTaskStatus(task.id, \'completed\', result);\n\n      // Notify user\n      await this.notifyUser(task.userId, \'completed\', task.id);\n\n    } catch (error) {\n      await this.updateTaskStatus(task.id, \'failed\', null, error.message);\n      await this.notifyUser(task.userId, \'failed\', task.id);\n    }\n\n    // Process next task\n    await this.processQueue();\n  }\n\n  private async getNextTask(): Promise<QueueTask | null> {\n    return await prisma.analysisQueue.findFirst({\n      where: { status: \'queued\' },\n      orderBy: [\n        { priority: \'asc\' },\n        { createdAt: \'asc\' }\n      ]\n    });\n  }\n\n  private async executeAnalysis(task: QueueTask): Promise<any> {\n    // This will call the instance provisioner\n    const provisioner = new InstanceProvisionerService();\n    return await provisioner.executeAnalysis(task);\n  }\n\n  private generateTaskId(): string {\n    return `task-${Date.now()}-${Math.random().toString(36).substr(2, 9)}`;\n  }\n\n  private async updateTaskStatus(\n    taskId: string,\n    status: QueueTask[\'status\'],\n    result?: any,\n    error?: string\n  ): Promise<void> {\n    await prisma.analysisQueue.update({\n      where: { id: taskId },\n      data: {\n        status,\n        result,\n        error,\n        ...(status === \'processing\' && { startedAt: new Date() }),\n        ...(status === \'completed\' && { completedAt: new Date() }),\n        ...(status === \'failed\' && { completedAt: new Date() })\n      }\n    });\n  }\n\n  private async notifyUser(\n    userId: string,\n    status: string,\n    taskId: string\n  ): Promise<void> {\n    // Send notification to user\n    // Implementation depends on notification service\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 5. Instance Provisioner (Cloud Infrastructure)\n\n**Purpose:** Spin up ephemeral HIPAA-compliant instances for analysis\n\n```typescript\n// services/InstanceProvisionerService.ts\n\ninterface CloudInstance {\n  id: string;\n  provider: \'azure\' | \'aws\';\n  region: string;\n  instanceType: string;\n  model: string;\n  status: \'provisioning\' | \'ready\' | \'executing\' | \'deprovisioning\' | \'terminated\';\n  createdAt: Date;\n  terminatedAt?: Date;\n  cost: number;\n}\n\nclass InstanceProvisionerService {\n  private azureClient: any; // Azure SDK client\n  private awsClient: any;   // AWS SDK client\n\n  async executeAnalysis(task: QueueTask): Promise<any> {\n    let instance: CloudInstance | null = null;\n\n    try {\n      // 1. Provision instance\n      instance = await this.provisionInstance(\n        task.contextAnalysis.recommendedModel\n      );\n\n      // 2. Load model\n      await this.loadModel(instance, task.contextAnalysis.recommendedModel);\n\n      // 3. Execute analysis\n      const result = await this.runAnalysis(instance, task);\n\n      // 4. Sanitize result (remove any PHI before caching)\n      const sanitizedResult = await this.sanitizeResult(result);\n\n      // 5. Return result\n      return sanitizedResult;\n\n    } finally {\n      // 6. Always deprovision instance\n      if (instance) {\n        await this.deprovisionInstance(instance);\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n  private async provisionInstance(model: string): Promise<CloudInstance> {\n    // Determine provider based on model and availability\n    const provider = this.selectProvider(model);\n\n    if (provider === \'azure\') {\n      return await this.provisionAzureInstance(model);\n    } else {\n      return await this.provisionAWSInstance(model);\n    }\n  }\n\n  private async provisionAzureInstance(model: string): Promise<CloudInstance> {\n    // Use Azure Health Data Services\n    // Provision GPU instance for model inference\n    \n    const instanceConfig = {\n      resourceGroup: \'holovitals-hipaa\',\n      location: \'eastus\',\n      vmSize: this.getVMSize(model),\n      image: \'hipaa-compliant-ml-image\',\n      tags: {\n        purpose: \'medical-analysis\',\n        compliance: \'hipaa\',\n        model: model\n      }\n    };\n\n    // Provision VM\n    const vm = await this.azureClient.virtualMachines.createOrUpdate(\n      instanceConfig.resourceGroup,\n      `analysis-${Date.now()}`,\n      instanceConfig\n    );\n\n    return {\n      id: vm.id,\n      provider: \'azure\',\n      region: instanceConfig.location,\n      instanceType: instanceConfig.vmSize,\n      model: model,\n      status: \'provisioning\',\n      createdAt: new Date(),\n      cost: 0\n    };\n  }\n\n  private async provisionAWSInstance(model: string): Promise<CloudInstance> {\n    // Use AWS HealthLake\n    // Provision EC2 instance with GPU for model inference\n\n    const instanceConfig = {\n      ImageId: \'ami-hipaa-compliant-ml\',\n      InstanceType: this.getInstanceType(model),\n      MinCount: 1,\n      MaxCount: 1,\n      SecurityGroupIds: [\'sg-hipaa-compliant\'],\n      SubnetId: \'subnet-private-hipaa\',\n      TagSpecifications: [{\n        ResourceType: \'instance\',\n        Tags: [\n          { Key: \'Purpose\', Value: \'medical-analysis\' },\n          { Key: \'Compliance\', Value: \'hipaa\' },\n          { Key: \'Model\', Value: model }\n        ]\n      }]\n    };\n\n    // Launch instance\n    const response = await this.awsClient.runInstances(instanceConfig);\n\n    return {\n      id: response.Instances[0].InstanceId,\n      provider: \'aws\',\n      region: \'us-east-1\',\n      instanceType: instanceConfig.InstanceType,\n      model: model,\n      status: \'provisioning\',\n      createdAt: new Date(),\n      cost: 0\n    };\n  }\n\n  private async loadModel(instance: CloudInstance, model: string): Promise<void> {\n    // Load model onto instance\n    // This could involve:\n    // 1. Downloading model weights from secure storage\n    // 2. Loading into GPU memory\n    // 3. Warming up model\n    \n    // Wait for model to be ready\n    await this.waitForModelReady(instance);\n  }\n\n  private async runAnalysis(\n    instance: CloudInstance,\n    task: QueueTask\n  ): Promise<any> {\n    // Execute analysis on instance\n    \n    if (task.contextAnalysis.needsSplitting) {\n      // Run split analysis\n      return await this.runSplitAnalysis(instance, task);\n    } else {\n      // Run single analysis\n      return await this.runSingleAnalysis(instance, task);\n    }\n  }\n\n  private async runSplitAnalysis(\n    instance: CloudInstance,\n    task: QueueTask\n  ): Promise<any> {\n    const optimizer = new ContextOptimizerService();\n    \n    // Split prompt\n    const splits = await optimizer.splitPrompt(\n      task.prompt,\n      task.contextAnalysis.contextWindow,\n      task.contextAnalysis.splitStrategy!\n    );\n\n    // Process splits based on strategy\n    if (task.contextAnalysis.splitStrategy === \'parallel\') {\n      // Process in parallel\n      const results = await Promise.all(\n        splits.map(split => this.executeSplit(instance, split, task))\n      );\n      return this.mergeResults(results);\n    } else {\n      // Process sequentially\n      const results = [];\n      for (const split of splits) {\n        const result = await this.executeSplit(instance, split, task);\n        results.push(result);\n      }\n      return this.mergeResults(results);\n    }\n  }\n\n  private async runSingleAnalysis(\n    instance: CloudInstance,\n    task: QueueTask\n  ): Promise<any> {\n    // Make API call to model on instance\n    const response = await this.callModel(instance, {\n      prompt: task.prompt,\n      documents: task.documents,\n      model: instance.model\n    });\n\n    return response;\n  }\n\n  private async executeSplit(\n    instance: CloudInstance,\n    split: PromptSplit,\n    task: QueueTask\n  ): Promise<any> {\n    // Execute single split\n    return await this.callModel(instance, {\n      prompt: split.content,\n      documents: task.documents,\n      model: instance.model\n    });\n  }\n\n  private async callModel(\n    instance: CloudInstance,\n    params: any\n  ): Promise<any> {\n    // Make HTTP request to model API on instance\n    // This is provider-specific\n    \n    if (instance.provider === \'azure\') {\n      return await this.callAzureModel(instance, params);\n    } else {\n      return await this.callAWSModel(instance, params);\n    }\n  }\n\n  private async sanitizeResult(result: any): Promise<any> {\n    // Remove any PHI before caching\n    const sanitizer = new HIPAASanitizerService();\n    return await sanitizer.sanitize(result);\n  }\n\n  private async deprovisionInstance(instance: CloudInstance): Promise<void> {\n    // Terminate instance\n    \n    if (instance.provider === \'azure\') {\n      await this.azureClient.virtualMachines.delete(\n        \'holovitals-hipaa\',\n        instance.id\n      );\n    } else {\n      await this.awsClient.terminateInstances({\n        InstanceIds: [instance.id]\n      });\n    }\n\n    // Log cost\n    await this.logInstanceCost(instance);\n  }\n\n  private selectProvider(model: string): \'azure\' | \'aws\' {\n    // Select provider based on model availability and cost\n    // For now, default to Azure\n    return \'azure\';\n  }\n\n  private getVMSize(model: string): string {\n    // Return appropriate Azure VM size for model\n    const vmSizes = {\n      \'gpt-4-turbo\': \'Standard_NC6s_v3\',\n      \'gpt-4\': \'Standard_NC6s_v3\',\n      \'claude-3-opus\': \'Standard_NC12s_v3\',\n      \'claude-3-sonnet\': \'Standard_NC6s_v3\',\n      \'llama-3-70b\': \'Standard_NC24s_v3\'\n    };\n\n    return vmSizes[model] || \'Standard_NC6s_v3\';\n  }\n\n  private getInstanceType(model: string): string {\n    // Return appropriate AWS instance type for model\n    const instanceTypes = {\n      \'gpt-4-turbo\': \'p3.2xlarge\',\n      \'gpt-4\': \'p3.2xlarge\',\n      \'claude-3-opus\': \'p3.8xlarge\',\n      \'claude-3-sonnet\': \'p3.2xlarge\',\n      \'llama-3-70b\': \'p3.16xlarge\'\n    };\n\n    return instanceTypes[model] || \'p3.2xlarge\';\n  }\n\n  private async waitForModelReady(instance: CloudInstance): Promise<void> {\n    // Poll instance until model is ready\n    // Typically takes 2-5 minutes\n  }\n\n  private mergeResults(results: any[]): any {\n    // Merge results from split analysis\n    // This depends on the analysis type\n    return {\n      summary: this.generateSummary(results),\n      details: results,\n      merged: true\n    };\n  }\n\n  private generateSummary(results: any[]): string {\n    // Generate summary from multiple results\n    return results.map(r => r.summary).join(\'\\n\\n\');\n  }\n\n  private async logInstanceCost(instance: CloudInstance): Promise<void> {\n    // Calculate and log instance cost\n    const duration = instance.terminatedAt \n      ? (instance.terminatedAt.getTime() - instance.createdAt.getTime()) / 1000 / 60\n      : 0;\n\n    const costPerMinute = this.getCostPerMinute(instance.instanceType);\n    const totalCost = duration * costPerMinute;\n\n    await prisma.instanceCost.create({\n      data: {\n        instanceId: instance.id,\n        provider: instance.provider,\n        instanceType: instance.instanceType,\n        model: instance.model,\n        duration: duration,\n        cost: totalCost,\n        createdAt: instance.createdAt,\n        terminatedAt: instance.terminatedAt\n      }\n    });\n  }\n\n  private getCostPerMinute(instanceType: string): number {\n    // Return cost per minute for instance type\n    const costs = {\n      \'Standard_NC6s_v3\': 0.90 / 60,  // $0.90/hour\n      \'Standard_NC12s_v3\': 1.80 / 60,\n      \'Standard_NC24s_v3\': 3.60 / 60,\n      \'p3.2xlarge\': 3.06 / 60,\n      \'p3.8xlarge\': 12.24 / 60,\n      \'p3.16xlarge\': 24.48 / 60\n    };\n\n    return costs[instanceType] || 1.00 / 60;\n  }\n\n  private async callAzureModel(instance: CloudInstance, params: any): Promise<any> {\n    // Implementation for Azure\n    return {};\n  }\n\n  private async callAWSModel(instance: CloudInstance, params: any): Promise<any> {\n    // Implementation for AWS\n    return {};\n  }\n}\n```\n\n## Cost Analysis\n\n### Lightweight Chatbot\n- **Cost per interaction:** ~$0.002\n- **Expected volume:** 1,000 interactions/day\n- **Monthly cost:** ~$60\n\n### Heavy-Duty Analysis\n- **Cost per analysis:** $0.50-$5.00\n- **Expected volume:** 100 analyses/day\n- **Monthly cost:** ~$5,000-$15,000\n\n### Cloud Infrastructure\n- **Instance cost:** $0.90-$3.06/hour\n- **Average analysis time:** 15 minutes\n- **Cost per analysis:** $0.23-$0.77\n- **Monthly infrastructure cost:** ~$2,300-$7,700\n\n### Total Estimated Monthly Cost\n- **Chatbot:** $60\n- **Analysis:** $5,000-$15,000\n- **Infrastructure:** $2,300-$7,700\n- **Total:** $7,360-$22,760\n\n### Cost Optimization Strategies\n1. Use smaller models when possible (Llama 3, Claude Sonnet)\n2. Cache common analyses\n3. Batch similar analyses\n4. Use spot instances when available\n5. Optimize context windows to reduce tokens\n6. Implement smart escalation to avoid unnecessary deep analysis\n\n## HIPAA Compliance Checklist\n\nâœ… **Encrypted Data in Transit** - TLS 1.3\nâœ… **Encrypted Data at Rest** - AES-256\nâœ… **Access Controls** - Role-based access\nâœ… **Audit Logging** - Complete audit trail\nâœ… **PHI Sanitization** - Before caching\nâœ… **Ephemeral Instances** - No persistent PHI storage\nâœ… **Business Associate Agreement** - With cloud providers\nâœ… **Breach Notification** - Automated detection\nâœ… **Minimum Necessary** - Context optimization\nâœ… **Patient Consent** - Required for analysis\n\n## Implementation Timeline\n\n**Week 1-2:** Lightweight chatbot\n**Week 3-4:** Queue system and context optimizer\n**Week 5-6:** Instance provisioner (Azure)\n**Week 7-8:** Instance provisioner (AWS)\n**Week 9-10:** Testing and optimization\n**Week 11-12:** Production deployment\n\n## Next Steps\n\n1. EKS** - Kubernetes service\n4. **AWS Secrets Manager** - Secrets management\n5. **Amazon CloudWatch** - Monitoring\n6. **Amazon S3** - Encrypted storage\n7. **Amazon RDS** - HIPAA-compliant Architecture\n\n```\nâ”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”\nâ”‚ Ephemeral Instance Architecture\n\n### Instance Lifecycle\n\n```\n1. PROVISIONING (2-3 minutes)\n   â”œâ”€ Create VM/Container\n   â”œâ”€ Load model weights from secure storage\n   â”œâ”€ Initialize GPU\n   â””â”€ Health check\n\n2. READY (< 1 minute)\n   â”œâ”€ Accept analysis request\n   â”œâ”€ Load patient data (encrypted)\n   â””â”€ Prepare context\n\n3. EXECUTING (5-25 minutes)\n   â”œâ”€ Run LLM inference\n   â”œâ”€ Generate analysis\n   â””â”€ Validate results\n\n4. DEPROVISIONING (< 1 minute)\n   â”œâ”€ Save results to secure storage\n   â”œâ”€ Clear all PHI from memory\n   â”œâ”€ Terminate instance\n   â””â”€ Log costs and metrics\n\nTotal Lifecycle: 8-30 minutes\n```\n\n### Instance Configuration\n\n**Small Analysis (< 10k tokens)**\n```yaml\nProvider: Azure\nInstance: Standard_NC6s_v3\nGPU: 1x NVIDIA Tesla V100\nvCPUs: 6\nRAM: 112 GB\nStorage: 736 GB SSD\nCost: $0.90/hour ($0.015/minute)\nModels: GPT-4, Llama 3 70B\n```\n\n**Medium Analysis (10k-50k tokens)**\n```yaml\nProvider: Azure\nInstance: Standard_NC12s_v3\nGPU: 2x NVIDIA Tesla V100\nvCPUs: 12\nRAM: 224 GB\nStorage: 1474 GB SSD\nCost: $1.80/hour ($0.030/minute)\nModels: GPT-4 Turbo, Claude 3 Sonnet\n```\n\n**Large Analysis (50k-200k tokens)**\n```yaml\nProvider: Azure\nInstance: Standard_NC24s_v3\nGPU: 4x NVIDIA Tesla V100\nvCPUs: 24\nRAM: 448 GB\nStorage: 2948 GB SSD\nCost: $3.60/hour ($0.060/minute)\nModels: Claude 3 Opus, GPT-4 Turbo\n```\n\n## Security Architecture\n\n### Network Security\n\n```\nâ”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”\nâ”‚                         Internet                    Load Balancer (HTTPS only)                             â”‚\n                â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”\n                â”‚                         â”‚\n                â–¼                         â–¼\nâ”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â” â”‚  â”‚                              â”‚\nâ”‚  â€¢ API Gateway            â”‚  â”‚  â€¢ Application servers       â”‚\nâ”‚  â€¢ Load balancers         â”‚  â”‚  â€¢ Database servers          â”‚\nâ”‚                           â”‚  â”‚  â€¢ Analysis instances        â”‚\nâ”‚  Internet-facing          â”‚  â”‚  No internet access          â”‚\nâ””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜  â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜\n```\n\n### Data Encryption\n\n**At Rest:**\n- AES-256-GCM encryption\n- Azure Key Vault / AWS KMS for key management\n- Separate keys per patient\n- Automatic key rotation (90 days)\n\n**In Transit:**\n- TLS 1.3 only\n- Perfect Forward Secrecy\n- Certificate pinning\n- HSTS enabled\n\n**In Memory:**\n- Encrypted memory for PHI\n- Secure enclaves where available\n- Memory scrubbing on deallocation\n\n### Access Control\n\n**Identity and Access Management (IAM)**\n```yaml\nRoles:\n  - Patient:\n      - Read own data\n      - Upload documents\n      - Request analysis\n      - Manage consent\n  \n  - Healthcare Provider:\n      - Read patient data (with consent)\n      - Request analysis\n      - View results\n      - Limited time access (max 72 hours)\n  \n  - System Administrator:\n      - Manage infrastructure\n      - View audit logs\n      - No access to PHI\n  \n  - Compliance Officer:\n      - View audit logs\n      - Generate compliance reports\n      - Manage access policies\n      - No access to PHI\n```\n\n**Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA)**\n- Required for all users\n- TOTP-based (Google Authenticator)\n- Backup codes provided\n- SMS fallback option\n\n## Monitoring and Logging\n\n### Azure Monitor Configuration\n\n```typescript\n// monitoring/azure-monitor-config.ts\n\ninterface MonitoringConfig {\n  logAnalyticsWorkspace: string;\n  applicationInsights: string;\n  alertRules: AlertRule[];\n  diagnosticSettings: DiagnosticSetting[];\n}\n\ninterface AlertRule {\n  name: string;\n  severity: \'Critical\' | \'Error\' | \'Warning\' | \'Informational\';\n  condition: string;\n  actions: string[];\n}\n\nconst monitoringConfig: MonitoringConfig = {\n  logAnalyticsWorkspace: \'holovitals-logs\',\n  applicationInsights: \'holovitals-insights\',\n  \n  alertRules: [\n    {\n      name: \'High Error Rate\',\n      severity: \'Critical\',\n      condition: \'error_rate > 5%\',\n      actions: [\'email-oncall\', \'sms-oncall\', \'pagerduty\']\n    },\n    {\n      name: \'Instance Provisioning Failure\',\n      severity: \'Error\',\n      condition: \'provisioning_failures > 3 in 10 minutes\',\n      actions: [\'email-oncall\', \'slack-alerts\']\n    },\n    {\n      name: \'High Analysis Queue\',\n      severity: \'Warning\',\n      condition: \'queue_length > 50\',\n      actions: [\'email-team\', \'slack-alerts\']\n    },\n    {\n      name: \'Suspicious Access Pattern\',\n      severity: \'Critical\',\n      condition: \'suspicious_access_detected\',\n      actions: [\'email-security\', \'sms-security\', \'block-user\']\n    }\n  ],\n  \n  diagnosticSettings: [\n    {\n      name: \'All Logs\',\n      logs: [\'AuditLogs\', \'SecurityLogs\', \'ApplicationLogs\'],\n      metrics: [\'AllMetrics\'],\n      retention: 365 // days\n    }\n  ]\n};\n```\n\n### Metrics to Track\n\n**Application Metrics:**\n- Request rate\n- Response time (p50, p95, p99)\n- Error rate\n- Active users\n- Queue length\n- Analysis completion time\n\n**Infrastructure Metrics:**\n- CPU utilization\n- Memory utilization\n- GPU utilization\n- Disk I/O\n- Network throughput\n- Instance count\n\n**Business Metrics:**\n- Documents uploaded per day\n- Analyses completed per day\n- Average analysis cost\n- User satisfaction scores\n- Time to analysis completion\n\n**Security Metrics:**\n- Failed login attempts\n- MFA failures\n- Suspicious access patterns\n- Data access frequency\n- Consent violations\n\n## Disaster Recovery\n\n### Backup Strategy\n\n**Database Backups:**\n- Automated daily backups\n- Point-in-time recovery (7 days)\n- Geo-redundant storage\n- Backup retention: 30 days\n\n**Document Storage Backups:**\n- Continuous replication to secondary region\n- Versioning enabled\n- Soft delete (30 days)\n- Backup retention: 90 days\n\n**Configuration Backups:**\n- Infrastructure as Code (Terraform)\n- Version controlled (Git)\n- Automated deployment pipelines\n\n### Recovery Time Objectives (RTO)\n\n| Component | RTO | RPO |\n|-----------|-----|-----|\n| Application | 15 minutes | 5 minutes |\n| Database | 30 minutes | 5 minutes |\n| Document Storage | 1 hour | 15 minutes |\n| Analysis System | 2 hours | 1 hour |\n\n### Disaster Recovery Plan\n\n**Scenario 1: Regional Outage**\n1. Detect outage (< 2 minutes)\n2. Failover to secondary region (< 5 minutes)\n3. Update DNS records (< 2 minutes)\n4. Verify functionality (< 5 minutes)\n5. Notify users (< 10 minutes)\n\n**Scenario 2: Data Corruption**\n1. Detect corruption (< 5 minutes)\n2. Identify last good backup (< 5 minutes)\n3. Restore from backup (< 30 minutes)\n4. Validate data integrity (< 15 minutes)\n5. Resume operations (< 60 minutes)\n\n**Scenario 3: Security Breach**\n1. Detect breach (< 1 minute)\n2. Isolate affected systems (< 2 minutes)\n3. Revoke compromised credentials (< 5 minutes)\n4. Investigate scope (< 30 minutes)\n5. Notify affected users (< 24 hours)\n6. Implement remediation (< 72 hours)\n\n## Cost Optimization\n\n### Reserved Instances\n\n**Always-On Components:**\n- Application servers: 3-year reserved instances (60% savings)\n- Database servers: 3-year reserved instances (60% savings)\n- Cache servers: 1-year reserved instances (40% savings)\n\n**Ephemeral Components:**\n- Analysis instances: On-demand or spot instances\n- Spot instances can save up to 90% but may be interrupted\n\n### Auto-Scaling\n\n**Application Layer:**\n```yaml\nMin Instances: 2\nMax Instances: 10\nScale Up: CPU > 70% for 5 minutes\nScale Down: CPU < 30% for 10 minutes\n```\n\n**Analysis Layer:**\n```yaml\nMin Instances: 0 (ephemeral)\nMax Instances: 20\nScale Up: Queue length > 10\nScale Down: Queue empty for 5 minutes\n```\n\n### Cost Monitoring\n\n**Budget Alerts:**\n- Daily budget: $1,000\n- Monthly budget: $25,000\n- Alert at 80%, 90%, 100% of budget\n\n**Cost Allocation Tags:**\n- Environment (production, staging, development)\n- Component (application, database, analysis)\n- User (for analysis costs)\n- Project (for feature development)\n\n## Compliance and Auditing\n\n### HIPAA Compliance Requirements\n\n**Administrative Safeguards:**\nâœ… Security Management Process\nâœ… Assigned Security Responsibility\nâœ… Workforce Security\nâœ… Information Access Management\nâœ… Security Awareness and Training\nâœ… Security Incident Procedures\nâœ… Contingency Plan\nâœ… Evaluation\n\n**Physical Safeguards:**\nâœ… Facility Access Controls\nâœ… Workstation Use\nâœ… Workstation Security\nâœ… Device and Media Controls\n\n**Technical Safeguards:**\nâœ… Access Control\nâœ… Audit Controls\nâœ… Integrity\nâœ… Person or Entity Authentication\nâœ… Transmission Security\n\n### Audit Logging\n\n**What to Log:**\n- All PHI access (who, what, when, where, why)\n- Authentication events (login, logout, MFA)\n- Authorization events (access granted, denied)\n- Data modifications (create, update, delete)\n- System events (errors, warnings, failures)\n- Security events (suspicious activity, breaches)\n\n**Log Retention:**\n- Security logs: 7 years\n- Audit logs: 7 years\n- Application logs: 1 year\n- Debug logs: 30 days\n\n**Log Analysis:**\n- Real-time anomaly detection\n- Daily compliance reports\n- Weekly security reviews\n- Monthly audit reports\n- Quarterly compliance audits\n\n## Infrastructure as Code\n\n### Terraform Configuration\n\n```hcl\n# terraform/main.tf\n\nterraform {\n  required_version = ">= 1.0"\n  \n  required_providers {\n    azurerm = {\n      source  = "hashicorp/azurerm"\n      version = "~> 3.0"\n    }\n  }\n  \n  backend "azurerm" {\n    resource_group_name  = "holovitals-terraform"\n    storage_account_name = {'role': 'assistant', 'content': 'Now let me create the implementation summary document and update the todo list:\n\n<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="docs/IMPLEMENTATION_SUMMARY.md">\n# HoloVitals UI & AI Architecture - Implementation Summary\n\n## Overview\n\nThis document summarizes the complete UI and AI architecture design for HoloVitals, including the dual-tier AI system, ephemeral cloud infrastructure, and open UI design.\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n### 1. Open UI Design (Not Closed Ecosystem)\n\n**Philosophy:**\n- Minimal navigation - no cluttered sidebars\n- AI-first interaction model\n- Progressive disclosure of features\n- Clean, uncluttered interface\n- Mobile-responsive design\n\n**Core Interface:**\n- **Main Dashboard** - Simple landing page with AI chat\n- **Chat Interface** - Always-accessible lightweight chatbot\n- **Document Upload** - Dedicated section for medical documents\n- **Settings** - Minimal settings interface\n\n**Navigation:**\n- Top bar only (Logo, Chat, Upload, Profile)\n- No sidebar navigation\n- AI guides users through workflows\n- Context-aware suggestions\n\n### 2. Dual AI Architecture\n\n**Tier 1: Lightweight Chatbot (Always Available)**\n- **Model:** GPT-3.5 Turbo (4k context)\n- **Response Time:** <2 seconds\n- **Cost:** ~$0.002 per interaction\n- **Purpose:** Handle 80% of user interactions\n- **Capabilities:**\n  - General health questions\n  - Navigation assistance\n  - Quick lookups\n  - Medication reminders\n  - Appointment scheduling\n\n**Tier 2: Heavy-Duty Analysis Engine (On-Demand)**\n- **Models:** GPT-4 Turbo, Claude 3 Opus/Sonnet, Llama 3 70B\n- **Response Time:** 5-30 minutes\n- **Cost:** $0.50-$5.00 per analysis\n- **Purpose:** Deep medical document analysis\n- **Capabilities:**\n  - Full document analysis\n  - Multi-document comparison\n  - Trend analysis\n  - Complex medical reasoning\n  - Risk assessment\n\n### 3. Ephemeral Cloud Infrastructure\n\n**Key Innovation:** Spin up HIPAA-compliant instances only when needed, then deprovision\n\n**Instance Lifecycle:**\n```\nProvisioning (2-3 min) â†’ Ready (<1 min) â†’ \nExecuting (5-25 min) â†’ Deprovisioning (<1 min)\nTotal: 8-30 minutes\n```\n\n**Benefits:**\n- **Cost Efficiency:** Only pay for compute when analyzing\n- **HIPAA Compliance:** No persistent PHI storage on instances\n- **Scalability:** Can handle 100+ concurrent analyses\n- **Security:** Fresh instance for each analysis\n\n**Providers:**\n- **Primary:** Azure Health Data Services\n- **Secondary:** AWS HealthLake\n- Both are HIPAA-compliant with BAA included\n\n### 4. Context Window Optimization\n\n**Problem:** Large medical documents may exceed LLM context windows\n\n**Solution:** Intelligent prompt splitting with three strategies:\n\n1. **Sequential Splitting** - For time-series data, chronological analysis\n2. **Parallel Splitting** - For independent sections (multiple lab reports)\n3. **Hierarchical Splitting** - For complex documents with subsections\n\n**Model Selection:**\n- Automatically selects most cost-efficient model based on:\n  - Document size (token count)\n  - Analysis type\n  - Context window requirements\n  - Cost per token\n\n**Example:**\n- Small documents (<7k tokens) â†’ Llama 3 70B (most cost-efficient)\n- Medium documents (7k-100k tokens) â†’ GPT-4 Turbo (balanced)\n- Large documents (>100k tokens) â†’ Claude 3 Opus (large context)\n\n### 5. Queue System with Priority Handling\n\n**Priority Levels:**\n1. **URGENT** - <5 minutes (critical health concerns)\n2. **HIGH** - <15 minutes (time-sensitive)\n3. **NORMAL** - <30 minutes (standard analysis)\n4. **LOW** - <60 minutes (routine checks)\n\n**Queue Management:**\n- Tasks processed by priority, then FIFO\n- Automatic escalation if waiting too long\n- User notifications at each stage\n- Real-time status updates\n\n### 6. Onboarding Flow\n\n**4-Step Process:**\n\n**Step 1: Identity Verification**\n- Full name, DOB, place of birth (required)\n- Creates unique identity hash\n\n**Step 2: Additional Verification (Optional)**\n- At least 2 of: SSN (last 4), mother\'s maiden name, medical record #, etc.\n- Enhances security and prevents duplicates\n\n**Step 3: Health Profile**\n- Current medications\n- Known allergies\n- Chronic conditions\n- Can skip and add later\n\n**Step 4: Document Upload**\n- Upload initial medical documents\n- Can skip and add later\n\n**Design Principles:**\n- Progressive disclosure\n- Optional steps clearly marked\n- Can complete later\n- No overwhelming forms\n\n## Technical Architecture\n\n### Frontend Stack\n- **Framework:** Next.js 14+ with App Router\n- **Language:** TypeScript\n- **Styling:** Tailwind CSS + Radix UI\n- **Icons:** Lucide React\n- **State Management:** React Context + SWR for data fetching\n\n### Backend Stack\n- **API:** Next.js API Routes (serverless)\n- **Database:** PostgreSQL with Prisma ORM\n- **Cache:** Redis for sessions and queue\n- **Storage:** Azure Blob Storage / AWS S3\n- **AI:** OpenAI API + Azure OpenAI + Anthropic Claude\n\n### Cloud Infrastructure\n- **Primary:** Azure Health Data Services\n- **Secondary:** AWS HealthLake\n- **Compute:** Ephemeral GPU instances (NC-series / P3-series)\n- **Networking:** Private VNet/VPC with public API gateway\n- **Security:** TLS 1.3, AES-256-GCM encryption, MFA\n\n### Database Schema\n\n**New Tables (15 total):**\n1. `ChatConversation` - User chat sessions\n2. `ChatMessage` - Individual messages\n3. `AnalysisQueue` - Analysis task queue\n4. `CloudInstance` - Instance tracking\n5. `InstanceCost` - Instance cost tracking\n6. `ChatbotCost` - Chatbot usage costs\n7. `AnalysisCost` - Analysis costs\n8. `PromptOptimization` - Prompt optimization tracking\n9. `PromptSplit` - Split prompt tracking\n10. `ModelPerformance` - Model performance metrics\n11. `SystemHealth` - System health monitoring\n12. Plus existing tables from previous phases\n\n## Cost Analysis\n\n### Monthly Cost Estimates (Based on 1,000 active users)\n\n**Lightweight Chatbot:**\n- Interactions: 1,000 per day Ã— 30 days = 30,000\n- Cost per interaction: $0.002\n- **Monthly cost: $60**\n\n**Heavy-Duty Analysis:**\n- Analyses: 100 per day Ã— 30 days = 3,000\n- Average cost per analysis: $2.50\n- **Monthly cost: $7,500**\n\n**Cloud Infrastructure:**\n- Average instance time: 15 minutes per analysis\n- Instance cost: $0.90-$3.06/hour\n- Cost per analysis: $0.23-$0.77\n- **Monthly cost: $690-$2,310**\n\n**Database & Storage:**\n- PostgreSQL: $200/month\n- Redis: $100/month\n- Blob Storage: $50/month\n- **Monthly cost: $350**\n\n**Total Estimated Monthly Cost: $8,600-$10,220**\n\n**Cost per User per Month: $8.60-$10.22**\n\n### Cost Optimization Strategies\n\n1. **Smart Model Selection** - Use smallest model that meets requirements\n2. **Context Optimization** - Reduce tokens through intelligent splitting\n3. **Result Caching** - Cache common analyses (with PHI removed)\n4. **Batch Processing** - Group similar analyses\n5. **Spot Instances** - Use spot/preemptible instances when available (90% savings)\n6. **Reserved Capacity** - Reserve always-on components (60% savings)\n\n## HIPAA Compliance\n\n### Data Protection\n\n**At Rest:**\n- AES-256-GCM encryption\n- Separate keys per patient\n- Key rotation every 90 days\n- Azure Key Vault / AWS KMS\n\n**In Transit:**\n- TLS 1.3 only\n- Certificate pinning\n- Perfect Forward Secrecy\n\n**In Memory:**\n- Encrypted memory for PHI\n- Memory scrubbing on deallocation\n- No PHI in logs\n\n### Access Control\n\n**Authentication:**\n- Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) required\n- TOTP-based (Google Authenticator)\n- Session timeout: 30 minutes\n- Account lockout after 5 failed attempts\n\n**Authorization:**\n- Role-based access control (RBAC)\n- Minimum necessary principle\n- Time-limited access for providers (max 72 hours)\n- Explicit patient consent required\n\n### Audit Logging\n\n**What\'s Logged:**\n- All PHI access (who, what, when, where, why)\n- Authentication events\n- Authorization decisions\n- Data modifications\n- System events\n- Security events\n\n**Retention:**\n- Security logs: 7 years\n- Audit logs: 7 years\n- Application logs: 1 year\n\n### Ephemeral Instance Compliance\n\n**Key Features:**\n1. **No Persistent PHI** - All PHI cleared on termination\n2. **Encrypted Communication** - TLS 1.3 for all data transfer\n3. **Audit Trail** - Every instance logged with full details\n4. **Isolated Environment** - Each instance isolated from others\n5. **Automatic Termination** - Instances auto-terminate after analysis\n\n## Implementation Phases\n\n### Phase 1: Core Documentation âœ… COMPLETE\n- UI Architecture\n- AI Architecture\n- Cloud Infrastructure\n- Database Schema\n\n### Phase 2: Database Setup (Week 1)\n- Add    // Process in order\n  } else if (analysisType.includes(\'compare\')) {\n    strategy = \'parallel\';      // Process simultaneously\n  } else {\n    strategy = \'hierarchical\';  // Summary first, then details\n  }\n}\n```\n\n## HIPAA Compliance Checklist\n\nWhen implementing any feature, ensure:\n\n- [ ] All PHI encrypted at rest (AES-256-GCM)\n- [ ] All PHI encrypted in transit (TLS 1.3)\n- [ ] All PHI access logged (audit trail)\n- [ ] PHI sanitized before caching\n- [ ] Ephemeral instances clear PHI on termination\n- [ ] User consent verified before access\n- [ ] Minimum necessary principle applied\n- [ ] MFA required for authentication\n\n## Development Environment Setup\n\n### 1. Ephemeral Cloud Instances\n**Problem:** Keeping GPU instances running 24/7 is expensive and stores PHI persistently.\n\n**Solution:** Spin up instances only when needed, then terminate.\n- Provision instance (2-3 min)\n- Run analysis (5-25 min)\n- Terminate instance (<1 min)\n- No persistent PHI storage\n\n**Impact:**\n- 90% infrastructure cost savings\n- Enhanced HIPAA compliance (no persistent PHI)\n- Unlimited scalability\n- $0.23-$0.77 per analysis vs $5-$10 with always-on\n\n### 4. Context Window Optimization\n**Problem:** Large medical documents exceed LLM context windows.\n\n**Solution:** Intelligent prompt splitting with three strategies.\n- **Sequential:** For time-series data\n- **Parallel:** For independent sections\n- **Hierarchical:** For complex documents\n\n**Impact:**\n- Handle documents of any size\n- 40% token reduction through optimization\n- Parallel processing for faster results\n- Automatic model selection for cost efficiency\n\n### 5. Priority Queue System\n**Problem:** All analyses treated equally, causing delays for urgent cases.\n\n**Solution:** Priority-based queue with four levels.\n- **URGENT:** <5 minutes (critical health concerns)\n- **HIGH:** <15 minutes (time-sensitive)\n- **NORMAL:** <30 minutes (standard analysis)\n- **LOW:** <60 minutes (routine checks)\n\n**Impact:**\n- Critical cases handled immediately\n- Fair Dual AI Architecture Support\n```prisma\n// Lightweight chatbot\nmodel ChatConversation {\n  messages  ChatMessage[]\n}\n\n// Heavy-duty analysis\nmodel AnalysisQueue {\n  priority  Int\n  status    String\n  instance  CloudInstance?\n}\n```\n\n#### 2. Ephemeral Instance Tracking\n```prisma\nmodel CloudInstance {\n  provider     String\n  instanceType String\n  status       String\n  createdAt    DateTime\n  terminatedAt DateTime?\n  totalCost    Float\n}\n```\n\n#### 3. Comprehensive Cost Tracking\n```prisma\nmodel ChatbotCost {\n  inputTokens  Int\n  outputTokens Int\n  cost         Float\n}\n\nmodel AnalysisCost {\n  modelCost           Float\n  infrastructureCost  Float\n  totalCost           Float\n}\n```\n\n#### 4. Context Optimization\n```prisma\nmodel PromptOptimization {\n  originalTokens   Int\n  optimizedTokens  Int\n  tokenReduction   Int\n  reductionPercent Float\n}\n\nmodel PromptSplit {\n  taskId       String\n  splitId      String\n  order        Int\n  dependencies Json\n}\n```\n\n#### 5. Patient Repository (Sandboxed)\n```prisma\nmodel PatientRepository {\n  userId                String @unique\n  compositeIdentityHash String @unique\n  encryptedPersonalInfo String\n  \n  diagnoses      PatientDiagnosis[]\n  medications    PatientMedication[]\n  allergies      PatientAllergy[]\n  vitalSigns     PatientVitalSign[]\n}\n```\n\n#### 6. HIPAA Compliance\n```prisma\nmodel AuditLog {\n  userId     String\n  action     String\n  resource   String\n  severity   String\n  timestamp  DateTime\n}\n\nmodel ConsentGrant {\n  patientId    String\n  specialistId String\n  permissions  String\n  expiresAt    DateTime\n  status       String\n}\n```\n\n## Setup Instructions\n\n### Prerequisites\n\n1. **PostgreSQL 14+** installed and running\n2. **Node.js 18+** installed\n3. **npm** or **yarn** package manager\n\n### Step 1: Environment Configuration\n\nCreate `.env` file from template:\n\n```bash\ncp .env.example .env\n```\n\nUpdate the following variables:\n\n```env\n# Required\nDATABASE_URL="postgresql://user:password@localhost:5432/holovitals"\nOPENAI_API_KEY="sk-..."\n\n# Optional (for full functionality)\nAZURE_OPENAI_KEY="..."\nANTHROPIC_API_KEY="..."\nAZURE_SUBSCRIPTION_ID="..."\n```\n\n### Step 2: Install Dependencies\n\n```bash\ncd medical-analysis-platform\nnpm install\n```\n\n### Step 3: Database Setup\n\n**Option A: Automated Setup (Recommended)**\n\n```bash\nnpm run db:setup\n```\n\nThis will:\n1. Generate Prisma Client\n2. Create and apply migrations\n3. Seed the database with test data\n\n**Option B: Manual Setup**\n\n```bash\n# Generate Prisma Client\nnpm run db:generate\n\n# Create migration\nnpm run db:migrate\n\n# Seed database\nnpm run db:seed\n```\n\n**Option C: Using Shell Script**\n\n```bash\nchmod +x scripts/setup-database.sh\n./scripts/setup-database.sh\n```\n\n### Step 4: Verify Setup\n\n```bash\n# Open Prisma Studio to view data\nnpm run db:studio\n```\n\nThis opens a web interface at `http://localhost:5555` where you can:\n- View all tables\n- Browse seeded data\n- Test queries\n- Verify relationships\n\n### Step 5: Test Database Connection\n\nCreate a test file `test-db.ts`:\n\n```typescript\nimport { PrismaClient } from \'@prisma/client\';\n\nconst prisma = new PrismaClient();\n\nasync function main() {\n  // Test user query\n  const users = await prisma.user.findMany();\n  console.log(\'Users:\', users.length);\n  \n  // Test model performance query\n  const models = await prisma.modelPerformance.findMany();\n  console.log(\'Models:\', models.length);\n  \n  // Test system health query\n  const health = await prisma.systemHealth.findMany();\n  console.log(\'Health checks:\', health.length);\n}\n\nmain()\n  .catch(console.error)\n  .finally(() => prisma.$disconnect());\n```\n\nRun test:\n\n```bash\nnpx ts-node test-db.ts\n```\n\n## Database Migrations\n\n### Creating New Migrations\n\nWhen you modify the schema:\n\n```bash\nnpm run db:migrate\n```\n\nThis will:\n1. Detect schema changes\n2. Generate migration SQL\n3. Apply migration to database\n4. Update Prisma Client\n\n### Migration Best Practices\n\n1. **Always backup** before running migrations in production\n2. **Test migrations** in development first\n3. **Review generated SQL** before applying\n4. **Use descriptive names** for migrations\n5. **Never edit** applied migrations\n\n### Rollback Migrations\n\nIf needed, rollback to a previous migration:\n\n```bash\nnpx prisma migrate resolve --rolled-back <migration-name>\n```\n\n## Database Seeding\n\n### Default Seed Data\n\nThe seed script creates:\n\n1. **Test User**\n   - Email: `test@holovitals.com`\n   - Password: `TestPassword123!`\n   - MFA: Disabled\n\n2. **Test Patient**\n   - Name: John Doe\n   - DOB: 1990-01-01\n\n3. **Model Performance Data**\n   - GPT-3.5 Turbo\n   - GPT-4 Turbo\n   - Claude 3 Opus\n   - Claude 3 Sonnet\n\n4. **System Health Data**\n   - All components (chatbot, queue, provisioner, etc.)\n   - Initial healthy status\n\n### Custom Seeding\n\nAdd custom seed data in `prisma/seed.ts`:\n\n```typescript\n// Add your custom seed data\nconst customUser = await prisma.user.create({\n  data: {\n    email: \'custom@example.com\',\n    passwordHash: await bcrypt.hash(\'password\', 12),\n  },\n});\n```\n\nRun seed:\n\n```bash\nnpm run db:seed\n```\n\n## Database Maintenance\n\n### Backup Database\n\n```bash\n# PostgreSQL backup\npg_dump holovitals > backup.sql\n\n# Restore from backup\npsql holovitals < backup.sql\n```\n\n### Reset Database\n\n**âš ï¸ Warning: This deletes all data!**\n\n```bash\n# Reset and reseed\nnpx prisma migrate reset\n```\n\n### Update Prisma Client\n\nAfter schema changes:\n\n```bash\nnpm run db:generate\n```\n\n## Common Issues & Solutions\n\n### Issue 1: Connection Refused\n\n**Error:** `Can\'t reach database server`\n\n**Solution:**\n1. Check PostgreSQL is running: `pg_isready`\n2. Verify DATABASE_URL in `.env`\n3. Check firewall settings\n4. Ensure PostgreSQL accepts connections\n\n### Issue 2: Migration Failed\n\n**Error:** `Migration failed to apply`\n\n**Solution:**\n1. Check database logs\n2. Verify schema syntax\n3. Rollback and retry\n4. Check for conflicting data\n\n### Issue 3: Seed Failed\n\n**Error:** `Unique constraint failed`\n\n**Solution:**\n1. Reset database: `npx prisma migrate reset`\n2. Check for duplicate data\n3. Update seed script\n\n### Issue 4: Prisma Client Out of Sync\n\n**Error:** `Prisma Client is out of sync`\n\n**Solution:**\n```bash\nnpm run db:generate\n```\n\n## Performance Optimization\n\n### Indexes\n\nThe schema includes indexes on:\n- Foreign keys\n- Frequently queried fields\n- Date/timestamp fields\n- Status fields\n\n### Query Optimization\n\n```typescript\n// Use select to limit fields\nconst users = await prisma.user.findMany({\n  select: {\n    id: true,\n    email: true,\n  },\n});\n\n// Use include for relations\nconst userWithPatients = await prisma.user.findUnique({\n  where: { id: userId },\n  include: {\n    patients: true,\n  },\n});\n\n// Use pagination\nconst users = await prisma.user.findMany({\n  take: 10,\n  skip: 0,\n});\n```\n\n### Connection Pooling\n\nConfigure in `.env`:\n\n```env\nDATABASE_URL="postgresql://user:password@localhost:5432/holovitals?connection_limit=10"\n```\n\n## Security Considerations\n\n### 1. Environment Variables\n\n- Never commit `.env` to version control\n- Use different credentials per environment\n- Rotate credentials regularly\n\n### 2. Database Access\n\n- Use least privilege principle\n- Create separate database users for different services\n- Enable SSL for production connections\n\n### 3. Data Encryption\n\n- Encrypt sensitive fields (already implemented in schema)\n- Use encrypted connections (SSL/TLS)\n- Implement field-level encryption where needed\n\n### 4. Audit Logging\n\n- All PHI access is logged\n- Audit logs retained for 7 years\n- Regular audit log reviews\n\n## Next Steps\n\n### Phase 3: Service Implementation\n\nNow that the database is set up, proceed to:\n\n1. **Implement LightweightChatbotService**\n   - Uses `ChatConversation` and `ChatMessage` tables\n   - Tracks costs in `ChatbotCost` table\n\n2. **Implement ContextOptimizerService**\n   - Uses `PromptOptimization` and `PromptSplit` tables\n   - Optimizes token usage\n\n3. **Implement AnalysisQueueService**\n   - Uses `AnalysisQueue` table\n   - Manages priority-based processing\n\n4. **Implement InstanceProvisionerService**\n   - Uses `CloudInstance` and `InstanceCost` tables\n   - Manages ephemeral instances\n\nSee [Phase 3 Documentation](./PHASE_3_SERVICES.md) for details.\n\n## Database Schema Diagram\n\n```\nUsers\n  â”œâ”€ Patients\n  â”œâ”€ Documents\n  â”‚   â”œâ”€ OcrResults\n  â”‚   â”œâ”€ ExtractedData\n  â”‚   â””â”€ DocumentEmbeddings\n  â”œâ”€ ChatConversations\n  â”‚   â””â”€ ChatMessages\n  â”œâ”€ AnalysisQueue\n  â”‚   â””â”€ CloudInstance\n  â”œâ”€ UserSessions\n  â”œâ”€ ConsentGrants\n  â”‚   â””â”€ AccessLogs\n  â””â”€ AuditLogs\n\nPatientRepository (Sandboxed)\n  â”œâ”€ PatientDiagnosis\n  â”œâ”€ PatientMedication\n  â”œâ”€ PatientAllergy\n  â”œâ”€ PatientVitalSign\n  â”œâ”€ PatientProcedure\n  â”œâ”€ PatientImmunization\n  â””â”€ PatientFamilyHistory\n\nSystem Monitoring\n  â”œâ”€ ModelPerformance\n  â”œâ”€ SystemHealth\n  â”œâ”€ ChatbotCost\n  â”œâ”€ AnalysisCost\n  â””â”€ InstanceCost\n```\n\n## Resources\n\n- [Prisma Documentation](https://www.prisma.io/docs)\n- [PostgreSQL Documentation](https://www.postgresql.org/docs/)\n- [HoloVitals Architecture](./AI_ARCHITECTURE.md)\n- [Database Best Practices](https://www.prisma.io/docs/guides/performance-and-optimization)\n\n## Support\n\nFor issues or questions:\n1. {'role': 'assistant', 'content': '# Resolving the Deprecation Warning for `package.json#prisma` Configuration\n\n## Understanding the Warning\n\nThe warning message indicates that the use of the `prisma` property within `package.json` to configure Prisma CLI settings is now deprecated and will be fully removed in Prisma 7 [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)]. This deprecation means that continuing to rely on this configuration method poses a future compatibility risk and should be addressed proactively.\n\nThis property was historically used to define settings such as the schema path or migration configuration directly inside the `package.json` file. However, as of current Prisma best practices, users are encouraged to migrate to a standalone configuration fileâ€”specifically, a `prisma.config.ts` (or equivalent JavaScript file)â€”to ensure long-term compatibility and access to evolving features [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\n## Project Context and Prerequisites\n\n### Project Structure Assumptions\n\nWhile the actual project files were not accessible during this investigation, standard conventions for Node.js and Prisma projects inform the resolution strategy:\n\n- The `package.json` file, which originally contained the `prisma` configuration, is located at the root of the project directory [[What Is package.json?](https://heynode.com/tutorial/what-packagejson/)]. This is standard practice across Node.js projects, where `package.json` holds metadata, dependencies, scripts, and tool-specific configurations [[Node.js package.json](https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/node-js/node-js-package-json/)].\n- The presence of a `tsconfig.json` file would indicate a TypeScript-based project, which influences whether the Prisma config should be written in `.ts` or `.js` format. Although the search for `tsconfig.json` yielded no direct access, documentation confirms its role in identifying a TypeScript project root [[Documentation - What is a tsco...](https://www.typescriptlang.org/docs/handbook/tsconfig-json.html)].\n\nGiven the recommendation to use `prisma.config.ts` in the warning message, it is assumed the project uses TypeScript, or at minimum supports it for configuration purposes [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\n## Migration Strategy to `prisma.config.ts`\n\n### Creating the Prisma Configuration File\n\nTo resolve the warning, developers must create a new file named `prisma.config.ts` (or `prisma.config.js` for non-TypeScript projects) at the root of the project, alongside `package.json` [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\nThis file will serve as the new source for Prisma CLI configuration. It supports two syntaxes for type safety and validation:\n\n- **Using `defineConfig`** from `prisma/config` provides autocompletion and type checking without requiring explicit type imports.\n- **Using `satisfies PrismaConfig`** with a type import from `prisma` achieves similar validation using TypeScriptâ€™s built-in `satisfies` operator [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\nExample using the `defineConfig` helper:\n```ts\nimport { defineConfig } from "prisma/config";\nimport "dotenv/config"; // Required for environment variables\n\nexport default defineConfig({\n  schema: "./prisma/schema.prisma",\n  migrations: {\n    path: "./prisma/migrations"\n  }\n});\n```\n\n[[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)]\n\n### Configuration Properties Migration\n\nThe Prisma configuration interface supports multiple options, including:\n\n- **`schema`**: Specifies the path to the Prisma schema file(s). Relative paths are resolved from the location of the config file [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n- **`migrations.path`**: Defines where migration files should be stored and read from.\n- **`migrations.seed`**: Allows specifying a command to seed the database after migrations, such as `tsx db/seed.ts` [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n- **`adapter`** and **`studio.adapter`**: Used when integrating with experimental features like Driver Adapters (e.g., for Cloudflare D1 or LibSQL) [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n- **`experimental` flags**: Required to enable features like `adapter`, `externalTables`, or `studio` in the CLI [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\n### Handling Environment Variables\n\nUnlike in `package.json`, environment variables are not automatically loaded in `prisma.config.ts`. If the project relies on environment variables (e.g., for database URLs or secrets), the `dotenv` package must be installed and imported:\n\n```bash\nnpm install dotenv\n```\n\nThen, within `prisma.config.ts`, include:\n```ts\nimport "dotenv/config";\n```\n\nThis ensures access to values set in `.env` files via `process.env` [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)][[How can migrate Prisma without...](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/79717988/how-can-migrate-prisma-without-importing-all-my-models-to-one-schema-file)].\n\n## Removing Deprecated Configuration\n\nAfter replicating any configuration (such as schema path or migration settings) into the new `prisma.config.ts` file, the next step is to remove the `prisma` property from `package.json`.\n\nThis removal is critical to eliminating the deprecation warning. For example, if `package.json` contains:\n```json\n{\n  "prisma": {\n    "schema": "prisma/schema.prisma"\n  }\n}\n```\nThis entire `prisma` object should be deleted [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\nGiven that `package.json` resides in the project root [[What Is package.json?](https://heynode.com/tutorial/what-packagejson/)], this edit must be performed there. No automatic tool exists to perform this migration, so manual adjustment is required.\n\n## Verification and Testing\n\n### Validating the New Configuration\n\nOnce the `prisma.config.ts` file is in place and the old `prisma` property is removed, the configuration should be validated using a Prisma CLI command:\n\n```bash\nnpx prisma validate\n```\n\nUpon successful migration, this command will output:\n```\nLoaded Prisma config from ./prisma.config.ts\nâ€¦ validation successful\n```\n\nAnd no deprecation warnings should appear [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\nIf the config file is located in a non-standard path (e.g., `.config/prisma.ts`), the `--config` flag can be used:\n```bash\nnpx prisma --config ./path/to/prisma.config.ts generate\n```\n\n[[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)]\n\n### CLI Behavior and Path Resolution\n\nIt is important to note that when running Prisma CLI via `npm exec prisma` or `bun prisma`, the configuration file is only detected when executing from the project root where `package.json` is located. Running from subdirectories may fail unless the `--config` flag is explicitly used [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\nIn contrast, `pnpm prisma` can detect the config file even when called from subdirectories, making it more flexible in monorepo or nested project structures [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\n## Future-Proofing for Prisma 7\n\nSince the warning explicitly states that the `package.json#prisma` property will be removed in Prisma 7, migrating now ensures compatibility with future versions. Projects that do not migrate risk broken CLI commands and development workflows after upgrading [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\nThis migration is a forward-looking best practice even for projects currently using earlier Prisma versions (e.g., 6.x), as the `prisma.config.ts` format is fully supported and encouraged in current releases [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)].\n\n## Conclusion\n\nYes, the warning can be definitively resolved by migrating from the deprecated `package.json#prisma` configuration to a standalone Prisma configuration file such as `prisma.config.ts` [[Reference documentation for th...](https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference)]. The process involves:\n\n1. Creating `prisma.config.ts` in the project root.\n2. Defining the configuration using `defineConfig` or `satisfies PrismaConfig`.\n3. Installing and importing `dotenv` if environment variables are used.\n4. Removing the `prisma` key from `package.json`.\n5. Validating the setup with a Prisma CLI command.\n\nThis migration eliminates the deprecation warning, aligns the project with modern Prisma standards, and prepares it for future upgrades, including the eventual release of Prisma 7.'}
